<div id="review_114426730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114426730" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114426730?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-august-2010">zzread-august-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114426730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer988346960243980864">"I'm going to spend some time with a highlander," I announce to my husband as I try to find a quiet place to read in a house with 3 loud boys and a cat...I watch my husband raise his eyebrows, then here comes the eyeroll...but I just don't care. There is something about this series that calls to me.<br/><br/>And I can't tell you why. The books are basically formulaic -- <br/>(1)Our heroine is a virgin.<br/>(2)Our hero is gorgeous, sexy, large, and well endowed.<br/>(3)There is travel either to or from to Scotland or bot</span>
  <span id="freeText988346960243980864" style="display:none">"I'm going to spend some time with a highlander," I announce to my husband as I try to find a quiet place to read in a house with 3 loud boys and a cat...I watch my husband raise his eyebrows, then here comes the eyeroll...but I just don't care. There is something about this series that calls to me.<br /><br />And I can't tell you why. The books are basically formulaic -- <br />(1)Our heroine is a virgin.<br />(2)Our hero is gorgeous, sexy, large, and well endowed.<br />(3)There is travel either to or from to Scotland or both.<br />(4)There is fae magic or mischief.<br />(5)Our hero and heroine seem to get separated.<br />(6)There is a nice tearful reunion.<br />(7)There is a happily ever after. <br />Again, I don't care. It works for me.<br /><br />In this installment, the previously mischievious Adam gets sent to the human world without all of his fae powers. Adam is being punished for helping the MacKeltar brothers. He can still sift from place to place, but he is invisible to humans except for Gabrielle, a sidhe-seer. Gabrielle has been taught to avoid the fae and not let them know that she can see them. She spend a lot of time avoiding Adam, but he keeps reappearing until she agrees to help him. Need I add that Adam is devastatingly gorgeous and Gabrielle is attracted to him. A romance slowly develops between the two. <br /><br />Adam is being pursued by Darroc (hmmm...wonder if he will appear in the Fever series somewhere) and Adam and Gabrielle end up in Scotland at the MacKeltar's castle. I loved how this book showed the MacKeltar brothers' happily ever after with their women. <br /><br />Adam's character surprised me. I always thought of him as a trouble maker. I liked seeing the tender, vulnerable, and loving Adam. Gabrielle is one lucky girl. <br /><br />Looking forward to reading the next book in the series!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="988346960243980864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3286894598108957273" style="display:none">Adam Black... you trouble maker! Got yerself in deep this time.<br />Thank goodness for Gabrielle the Sidhe-seer (she sees the Fae while they walk amongst us invisible to most)!<br />Adam Black, the Fae prince is suffering his punishment under the Fae Queen. He is to be 'human' and mostly powerless until she forgives him. But there is more going on than she or even he knows.<br />He needs to contact her to plead forgiveness, but he is invisible to humans and the Fae are invisible to him. <br />Enter Gabrielle who has lived under the burden of being able to see the Fae her whole life. She's become quite adept at hiding her 'talent/curse' until she ogles Adam Black and all his beefy goodness. <br />Now he knows she sees him and is determined to get her to help him. <br />I loved how Gabby was so determined to not let him seduce her. She was seriously afraid for her life!<br />Adam is used to women falling at his feet, and he figures he knows just how to seduce a woman's help after over 1000 years of practice. But seducing Gabrielle will require him to become more emotionally involved than he is used to.<br />I liked how all the characters are fallible and quirky. There's also the cultural differences. Despite how much both Gabby and Adam think they know about each other's people, they don't know the half of it!<br />I LOVED the epilogue for this one. Honestly it was what gave the 5th star for me.<br /><br />I listened to this on audio and the reader, Phil Gigante, is fantastic as usual!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055814902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12633343694124523853"><b>5+++ stars</b><br/><br/><b>LOVED LOVED LOVED LOVED IT!</b><br/><br/>Loved the storyline, the <i>fae</i> references that tie back to the Fever series. Absolutely LOVED Adam Black!<br/><br/>Hands down, my absolute favorite in the series! I'm ending the series here since I don't think anything can top Adam Black!</span>

<div id="review_224428536" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224428536" />
    <a title="Nisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2451459-nisha"><img alt="Nisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473558883p2/2451459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224428536?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=alpha-heros">alpha-heros</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=faires-fae-fey">faires-fae-fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=dangerous-or-bad-boys">dangerous-or-bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=magical">magical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=hot-hero-award">hot-hero-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=bending-time">bending-time</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224428536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14887947195899828528">I'm not exactly sure why I've been avoiding to write a review for this book. Possibly because it feels so final that I've completed Adam Black's book. Anyway, this is one of those really good books that deserves a sparkling review, so here goes:<br/><br/>The book starts with our very favorite hero, Adam Black. Yes, the Fae who has meddled with countless human lives during the earlier books and is exceedingly arrogant under both Fae and human parameters. Anyway, he's an odd duck among the Fae since he actu</span>
  <span id="freeText14887947195899828528" style="display:none">I'm not exactly sure why I've been avoiding to write a review for this book. Possibly because it feels so final that I've completed Adam Black's book. Anyway, this is one of those really good books that deserves a sparkling review, so here goes:<br /><br />The book starts with our very favorite hero, Adam Black. Yes, the Fae who has meddled with countless human lives during the earlier books and is exceedingly arrogant under both Fae and human parameters. Anyway, he's an odd duck among the Fae since he actually likes the humans (even while he thinks himself far superior than them) and speaks in support of them on multiple occasions. The Seelie Queen, Aoibheal, has had enough of it and punishes Adam to live as an invisible human. This is tragic for the great Adam Black since a, he's lost all his awesome godly powers, b, he's gotta eat and sleep, and c, he's got no one to show off to and pass his time. So, Adam Black wallows in self-pity (sorta) until he meets Gabrielle, a law-student who happens to suffer from an affliction - she can see the Fae, even through their glamor. And so, Gabielle happens to be the only person who can see and help Adam Black. Of course, Gabrielle isn't too keen about helping Adam. Eventually, they are forced to work together to save the Seelie Queen from the threat of Darroc (the 'Lord Master' *snicker* from the Fever series).<br /><br />Adam Black is ridiculously hot. In fact, at times, I don't even care about the story because I love learning about him, talking about him, seeing how his mind works. Gabrielle is a pretty awesome heroine. In fact, I like her the best - compared to Gwen and Chloe. It's funny how she fights her attraction to the Fae.<br /><br />I loved the chemistry between Adam and Gabrielle - and their love scenes were *fans self* plain whoa. <br /><br />I don't have much else to say because it was so fun and I just loved it. I've already read the Fever series, it was kinda cool to read about how Darroc was cursed and Aoibheal pre-disappearance days. Overall, I highly recommend this book. I would advise everyone to read the Drustan and Dageus's book first - which is great for the story build-up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14887947195899828528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IBIIk02Z+BwVFkL4tHHvGH4589exjcE+C5eNjSrUFDQzCoyRSaCsKXvBmQ9tIJbDRMeQwyIj8b2qZTKUZpPZ5A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V8xH8vBxQp3VCpRhzdB+CGfLo5QaZBMScQ/HZtdYm+pE1MPw9EgWqLvdT5YUgQfTXTXAgInKI5HQ/Xh/mx9WOg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10514318445787093844">“The only other calling I ever felt was an irrepressible desire to be Captain of my own Starship. I was born in the wrong century and it wasn’t possible, so I chose to explore the universe by writing fiction instead. Books are doors to endless adventure.” -KMM<br/><br/>Karen Marie Moning is the #1 NYT bestselling author of the Fever Series and Highlander novels.<br/><br/>An alum of the Immaculate Conception Academy, </span>
  <span id="freeText10514318445787093844" style="display:none">“The only other calling I ever felt was an irrepressible desire to be Captain of my own Starship. I was born in the wrong century and it wasn’t possible, so I chose to explore the universe by writing fiction instead. Books are doors to endless adventure.” -KMM<br /><br />Karen Marie Moning is the #1 NYT bestselling author of the Fever Series and Highlander novels.<br /><br />An alum of the Immaculate Conception Academy, at seventeen she attended Purdue University where she completed a BA in Society &amp; Law, with minors in Philosophy, Creative Writing and Theatre, while working full time as a bartender and computer consultant. She intended to go to law school but after an internship with a firm of Criminal Attorneys, decided against it. For the next decade, she worked in insurance, where she wrote intercompany arbitrations and directed commercial litigation. At the age of thirty, she decided it was time to get serious and do what she’d always wanted to do: write fiction novels.<br /><br />Beyond the Highland Mist was published in 1999 and nominated for two RITA awards. She then published six more novels in her award-winning HIGHLANDER series, and received the RITA Award in 2001 for The Highlander’s Touch.<br /><br />In 2004, she began writing the #1 New York Times bestselling FEVER series. The books have been optioned twice for potential franchise development by Twentieth Century Fox and DreamWorks Studios, but the rights are currently held by Moning who has expressed a desire to one day see it as a television series. Her novels have been published in over thirty countries. She divides her time between Ohio and Florida and is working on two future projects for Random House Publishing.<br /><br />“I have always imagined that Paradise will be a kind of library.” – Jorge Luis Borges</span>
